<Rate>4</Rate>< review>
Usually go this place for volunteering for packing fruits and vegetables that will be distributed to the people with less affordability. Nice place. Any one can sign up to volunteer on any day. Usually it's 3 house volunteership. They give you a break after the first one and half hour for half hour followed by another hour of volunteering. They divide people based on the work example boxes preparation, packing, carrying the packed boxes to the weighing area and arranging the weigehd boxes. We can choose any task that we would like to pick. During the break they do offer some snacks and beverages. They have light music on and chatting with friends and volunteering is fun ðŸ˜ƒ.< /review>

<rate>4<//rate>< text>
This is a central distribution center and warehouse but they do not have people come to this location to pick up food.

To get food from Second Harvest you need to call the main phone number and they will tell you what bank is closest to you, also this is based on the day of the week. Banks  vary in the amount of food they provide and the quality of the food. For example, if you live downtown, they will likely send you to North 4th Street, the Salvation Army. They provide a very small bag of items for one person. You have to register at all of the banks, sign up give your name and ID the first time you show up. You don't need to show ID later.< /text>

< Text>
I absolutely enjoyed my experience at I love Lulu Hair Spa Saturday, April 15, 2021. I recently moved to Studio City March 2021, and I couldn't wait to get back to a good regimen for my hair. I found this gem online. After watching a Youtube video of Lulu and her sister, reading the reviews, and viewing the website -  I got excited. I like how Lulu is from North Carolina and just really intune to hair and making people feel good about their hair. Her sister was icing on the cake when stated she wants you to come in feeling one way and leaving feeling totally different in a good way. I definitely felt my hair/scalp was fully nurtured. I have a lot going on with my hair - breakage, thinning and just a need of some really good products to get me back on track. I am excited to see what my hair will feel and look like in about 4 months. The whole vibe of the decor, cleanliness, professionalism, and the comfort was pluses for me. The only One thing I didn't like - you see a different stylist each time you book an appointment unless you pay $25 add'l to the service amounts for a request. I don't understand why. I did ask and the answer I received, it's a better workflow and we all use the same products. I still can't wrap my brain around it and I like the idea of seeing the same person. I do understand each stylist uses the same product and nothing would be different other than a cut, color, or certain style. But none of that deter me from wanting to come back. The good definitely outweighs that one dislike. I have my next appointment in two weeks, so we shall see. Wish me success!< /Text>

< Text>
If I could give negative stars I would. I was sooo excited and ready to fall in love with this place.  I thought I found my new salon home. Organic Black Hair Salon,  so LA, so amazing,  like finding a needle in a haystack!

All the ambiance and organic products don't mean anything if you can't/don't thoroughly communicate your services to a new client.

For one,  it should be called a "wet bar" since ALL the employees are too oblivious to communicate to NEW clients that if you want your hair dried, that they have to factor in time for that in your appointment.

And if they're about to close, they will have you walk out with a fully wet head [even though you communicate repeatedly YOU would NEVER do that] bc they can't be bothered to dry your hair bc they want to go home. REALLLY?!

You don't think it's IMPORTANT to communicate that to a brand new client who asked for a consultation BEFORE you wet their massive thick head of hair [they told you they always wear their hair straight]?!?!

And then there's 30 minutes left until "closing time"& you'd rather argue with the client over a technicality, instead of righting the wrong.  And then the manager comes in and commences to argue with me about how I can leave with a wet head and come back another day at their convenience.  So now instead of wasting 30 minutes of my time,  you've now wasted OVER an hour about how you "can't".

In the hour they spent arguing with me,  thru could've been drying my hair!

Sadly,  this is one of the reasons why so many black owned businesses do not thrive.  As a business owner, don't argue with a customer.  Take full accountability for YOUR STAFF being UNCLEAR,  by not communicating to a new customer how their salon works.  It's YOUR responsibility to 'dummy proof' any new client to properly manage expectations.  YOU give the client ALL of the information they need so they can make  FULLY INFORMED decision prior to receiving services.  Don't refer to your staff's LACK of communication as "client/staff 'miscommunication'". And right the wrong at the client's convenience, not yours.

I shell out tons of money for my hair, I shouldn't have to argue to pay someone to finish doing my damn hair.

I was ready to arrange a whole day with me and my gfs to go and have the place to ourselves. Instead,  I'm writing a review after driving home,  pissed and staying up 2 hours untangling, drying,  and straightening my own hair. #Wasteoftime</Text>

<text>I Hate Lulu's
I went in to get a root coloring (greys); A trim and deep conditioning. First off, on a positive note, it's a lovely atmosphere. Clean facility and soothing music. BUT IT ENDS THERE
I was met by a cosmetology STUDENT who informed me that she was still working on her HOURS (!!???) I regret stopping services not because she wasn't African American BUT because she told me that she was a "work in progress"...SMH--Who wants a work in progress working on their head? I mean these are a la carte  salon prices. $65 for root coloring; $60 for cut; $35 for deep conditioning (which consists of olive oil added to conditioner and being place under a "steam machine"; $15 dollars for a blow dry (if you don't want your hair cut wet) $175 in total.
After the student colored my hair and conditioned my hair. The other services were performed by another young lady--who did the blow dry and cut (cut was not "precision" as advertised). It infuriates me that the second young lady in my head failed to inform me that the grays (that she watched the student cover) were still very visible.

< Review>
Giving it a three.
The two women that work throughout the week can make good burgers. They don't seem to be very family friendly. They also tend to make very thin and burnt pizzas and flavorless fries.
I am really hoping these two women aren't the ones that run the place.
If so...I believe the man that works generally on the weekends should get handed the business. That man is what makes this place. He is very polite and playful when we come with our kids. His food is wonderful and he is a man of great seasoning skills.

My recommendations are either hand the business to him full-time or (to the customers) ONLY COME ON THE WEEKENDS.< /Review>

<Review>If you want the best traditional Southern California Mexican food, this is it. This place has been here for decades in Banning, CA. Family owned and operated, what sets this place apart from a lot of the other hometown favorite Mexican food restaurants is that this place is always clean. That, and the fact that their specialty, the "Green Burrito", will light you up! They have a thermometer next to the order window that displays how much heat the green burritos have each day.  While ordering, you can look into a kitchen that is kept clean and tidy.  The parking lot is small, so be prepared to park on the street. It is worth giving a try.</Review><Pics>None< /Pics>< username>

<Rating>5<//Rating><Text>You don't want to wait until the end of the day to eat the best Mexican food in town,  they take last orders around 6pm. They are in the kitchen bright & early, & this kitchen is run like a well oiled machine. Clean, "A" rated!

plastic utensils.
Just hot delicious Mexican food!
You order at the window and they bring it to your table. Sitting is sparse, one long communal table and a  few side tables that accommodate 4 guests each.

<UserId.>117972306235366027327</UserId.><user_name>Kati Millett<//user_name><Date>1558393597844<//Date><rate>5</rate>< text>
Best Mexican food for miles. Literally miles, we live in the high desert. We always plan ahead to make time to stop there.
I recommend eating there because then you get the best chips and salsa ever! It's made with fresh tomatoes and cilantro. It's so good you could easily spoil your lunch on it.
Let's talk about the chile verde it is hot. I'm talking smoke out the ears, red crying eyes, red face, runny nose, breathing flames HOT. But oh so worth it! They even have a thermometer above the order window of how hot it is today. It's so good!
They have the best fresh tomatoes! They use them as a garnish, but if you take a little time to sprinkle on some salt and eat them, they will send you heaven.
So to some it up, yes I would eat here if I were you.<//text>
